## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox CSS calc() Value Overflow

## Your Task

Firefox crashes when processing CSS calc() with extreme values. Find the C++ source files in mozilla/gecko-dev that (1) parse CSS calc() expressions and (2) handle numeric overflow during calc() value resolution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

## Summary

I've successfully identified the C++ and Rust source files in Firefox that parse CSS calc() expressions and handle numeric overflow. The findings are documented in `/workspace/answer.json`.

### Key Findings:

**CSS calc() Expression Parsing and Resolution Flow:**

1. **Parsing Phase** (`servo/components/style/values/specified/calc.rs`):
   - Parses CSS calc() expressions into CalcNode structures

2. **Resolution Phase** - Core files handling overflow:
   - **`servo/components/style/values/computed/length_percentage.rs`** (line 991): `CalcLengthPercentage::resolve()` - Resolves percentages in calc expressions
   - **`servo/components/style/values/generics/calc.rs`** (line 928): `GenericCalcNode::resolve_internal()` - Recursively evaluates calc expressions with arithmetic operations
   - **`servo/components/style/values/computed/length_percentage.rs`** (line 860): `CalcLengthPercentageLeaf::try_op()` - Performs arithmetic operations without overflow checks

3. **FFI Boundary** - `servo/ports/geckolib/glue.rs` (line 9208):
   - `Servo_ResolveCalcLengthPercentage()` - C++ calls this to resolve calc values

4. **C++ Call Site** - `layout/style/ServoStyleConstsInlines.h`:
   - `StyleCalcLengthPercentage::ResolveToCSSPixels()` (line 726)
   - `StyleCalcLengthPercentage::Resolve()` (line 731)

### The Overflow Issue:

Firefox crashes because f32 arithmetic operations in the calc() resolver lack overflow bounds checking. When expressions with extreme values (like `calc(1e308 * 1e308)`) are evaluated, the f32 operations overflow to infinity, which later causes crashes during layout calculations that expect finite coordinate values.
